  [1mFull Model Response Summary[22m

  The GPT OSS 120B model successfully analyzed the project after reading
  README.md and provided the following comprehensive explanation:

  [1mProject Overview – terminalcp[22m

  [1mPurpose[22m: terminalcp lets AI agents (or any program) control interactive
  command-line tools just like a human would. It's essentially "Playwright
  for the terminal": the agent can start a process, send keystrokes, read
  output, and keep the session alive, all while preserving full terminal
  emulation (colors, cursor movement, etc.).

  [1mKey capabilities[22m:
  • [1mDebugging[22m – drive LLDB, GDB, pdb, etc.
  • [1mAI-to-AI[22m – run other AI assistants (Claude, Gemini, etc.) as
  subprocesses.
  • [1mREPL / shell[22m – interact with Python, Node, Ruby REPLs, DB shells,
  system monitors.
  • [1mGeneral CLI[22m – any interactive CLI that expects human input.
  • [1mMultiple processes[22m – run many sessions simultaneously without blocking.
  • [1mAttach[22m – users can attach to AI-spawned sessions from their own
  terminal (like screen/tmux) to watch or help.

  [1mTwo output modes[22m:
  • [1mTerminal mode (stdout)[22m – returns the full rendered screen (good for
  TUIs, debuggers).
  • [1mStream mode[22m – raw output, optional ANSI stripping, incremental reading
  (good for logs, builds).

  [1mArchitecture[22m:
  1. [1mTerminalManager[22m – core library that creates PTY sessions (via
  node-pty), handles I/O, ANSI, and provides the API.
  2. [1mTerminalServer[22m – background process that holds all sessions, listening
   on a Unix-socket (~/.terminalcp/server.socket). Sessions persist across
  client disconnects.
  3. [1mTerminalClient[22m – used by both the CLI and the MCP server to talk to
  the server over the socket.
  4. [1mUser interfaces[22m – MCP server (exposes a single terminalcp tool) and a
  CLI (terminalcp command). Both use the same client-server protocol.

  [1mMCP usage[22m – send JSON commands (e.g.,
  [38;2;177;185;249m{"action":"start","command":"python3 -i","name":"py"}[39m) to start/stop
  processes, send input (stdin), get output (stdout/stream), list sessions,
   etc.

  [1mCLI usage[22m – [38;2;177;185;249mterminalcp start <name> "<command>"[39m, [38;2;177;185;249mterminalcp stdin <name> [39m
  "cmd" ::Enter, [38;2;177;185;249mterminalcp stdout <name>[39m, [38;2;177;185;249mterminalcp stream <name> [39m
  --since-last, etc.

  [1mTypical use-cases[22m:
  • Debug code step-by-step with LLDB/GDB.
  • Run other AI agents as subprocesses.
  • Drive REPLs, database shells, or any interactive TUI.
  • Monitor long-running builds or logs.
  • Attach from a real terminal to watch or intervene in AI-spawned
  sessions.

  [1mDevelopment[22m:
  • npm install → install deps.
  • npm run build → build.
  • npm test → run tests.

  [1mLicense[22m – MIT.
